    <section class="primary-container">
     <div class="page-width-container">
      <div class="main-content">
       <article class="article page" itemscope="" sc-render-smart-button="false">
        <section class="article-container" data-stats-ve="35">
         <h1>
          How to download your Google data
         </h1>
         <div class="article-content-container">
          <div class="cc">
           <p>
            <strong>
             Important:
            </strong>
            If you download your Google data, it doesn’t delete it from Google’s servers. Learn
            <a href="/accounts/answer/32046">
             how to delete your account
            </a>
            or
            <a href="/websearch/answer/465">
             how to delete your activity
            </a>
            .
           </p>
           <div>
            <p>
             You can export and download your data from the Google products you use, such as your:
            </p>
            <ul>
             <li>
              Email
             </li>
             <li>
              Documents
             </li>
             <li>
              Calendar
             </li>
             <li>
              Photos
             </li>
             <li>
              YouTube videos
             </li>
             <li>
              Data about registration and account activity
             </li>
            </ul>
            <p>
             You can create an archive to keep for your records or use the data in another service.
            </p>
           </div>
           <div>
            <strong>
             Important
            </strong>
            : If actions are deemed risky, to protect your account, they may be delayed or unavailable.
           </div>
           <div>
            <strong>
             Tip:
            </strong>
            If you can't find some of your videos, check if you have a
            <a href="/accounts/answer/7001996" rel="noopener">
             Brand Account
            </a>
            . If so, you may need to
            <a href="/accounts/answer/3024190#YouTube_videos1" rel="noopener">
             switch accounts
            </a>
            .
           </div>
           <h2>
            Step 1: Select data to include in your download archive
           </h2>
           <div>
            <ol>
             <li>
              Go to the
              <a href="https://takeout.google.com/" rel="noopener" target="_blank">
               Download your data
              </a>
              page. Google products that have your data are automatically selected.
              <ul>
               <li>
                If you don’t want to download data from a product, uncheck the box beside it.
               </li>
               <li>
                If you only want to download some of your data from a product, you may have the option to select a button like
                <img alt="List" height="24" src="//lh3.googleusercontent.com/0HZmF-PjS6LzUGN4aXEFbNo_hbtIJxWbjDL9ya6dDY7hWcWKElyRQOhddmKb1WFxqp94=w24" title="List" width="24"/>
                All data included. Then, you can uncheck the box next to data you don’t want to include.
               </li>
              </ul>
             </li>
             <li>
              Select
              <strong>
               Next step
              </strong>
              .
             </li>
            </ol>
           </div>
           <div>
            <strong>
             Important:
            </strong>
            The file may not include changes made to your data between when you request a download and when your archive is created.
            <a href="/accounts/answer/3024190#recent_changes" rel="noopener">
             Learn more about what may not be included
            </a>
            .
           </div>
           <h2>
            Step 2: Customize your archive format
           </h2>
           <h3>
            Delivery method
           </h3>
           <h4 class="zippy">
            Send download link via email
           </h4>
           <div>
            <div>
             <p>
              We'll email you a link to download your Google data archive.
             </p>
             <ol>
              <li>
               For "Delivery method," select
               <strong>
                Send download link via email
               </strong>
               .
              </li>
              <li>
               Select
               <strong>
                Create export
               </strong>
               .
              </li>
              <li>
               In the email that arrives, select
               <strong>
                Download archive
               </strong>
               .
              </li>
              <li>
               To download your Google data, follow the steps on the screen.
              </li>
             </ol>
            </div>
           </div>
           <h4 class="zippy">
            Add to Drive
           </h4>
           <div>
            <div>
             <p>
              We'll add your archive to
              <a href="https://drive.google.com/" rel="noopener" target="_blank">
               Google Drive
              </a>
              and email you a link to its location. Your data will count toward
              <a href="https://drive.google.com/settings/storage" rel="noopener" target="_blank">
               your storage
              </a>
              .
             </p>
             <ol>
              <li>
               For "Delivery method," select
               <strong>
                Add to Drive
               </strong>
               .
              </li>
              <li>
               Select
               <strong>
                Create export
               </strong>
               .
              </li>
              <li>
               In the email that arrives, select
               <strong>
                View in Drive
               </strong>
               . You'll see a folder with your data organized by product.
              </li>
              <li>
               To download your data, at the top of the screen, select Download
               <img alt="Download" height="24" src="//lh3.googleusercontent.com/eRYotoZH_XOCfl8BMAXQs0JhVoRMJrVZTIOdA6maEyZ6tXnSsBT9hdWRMGJhtVmJ0jo=w24" title="Download" width="24"/>
               .
              </li>
             </ol>
            </div>
           </div>
           <h4 class="zippy">
            Add to Dropbox
           </h4>
           <div>
            <div>
             <p>
              We'll upload your archive to
              <a href="https://www.dropbox.com/" rel="noopener" target="_blank">
               Dropbox
              </a>
              and email you a link to its location.
             </p>
             <ol>
              <li>
               For "Delivery method," select
               <strong>
                Add to Dropbox
               </strong>
               .
              </li>
              <li>
               Select
               <strong>
                Link accounts and create export
               </strong>
               .
              </li>
              <li>
               You'll be directed to Dropbox. Sign in to your Dropbox account if prompted.
              </li>
              <li>
               In the Dropbox window that asks if Google Download Your Data can access its own "Apps" folder in your Dropbox, select
               <strong>
                Allow
               </strong>
               .
              </li>
              <li>
               To keep your data private, make sure you're not sharing this Dropbox folder with anyone else.
              </li>
              <li>
               In the email that arrives, select
               <strong>
                View in Dropbox
               </strong>
               . You'll be taken to the Dropbox folder with your archive.
              </li>
              <li>
               To download your data, follow Dropbox's process to download files.
              </li>
             </ol>
            </div>
            <div>
             <p>
              <strong>
               Notes
              </strong>
             </p>
             <ul>
              <li>
               After you follow these steps, Google Download Your Data will show up in your Dropbox security settings as a linked app. You can remove Google as a linked app at any time. (If you export data to Dropbox in the future, you'll need to give Google access again.)
              </li>
              <li>
               When your archive reaches Dropbox, Google is no longer responsible for it. Your archive will be covered by the
               <a href="https://www.dropbox.com/terms" rel="noopener" target="_blank">
                Dropbox Terms of Service
               </a>
               .
              </li>
             </ul>
            </div>
           </div>
           <h4 class="zippy">
            Add to Microsoft OneDrive
           </h4>
           <div>
            <div>
             <p>
              We'll upload your archive to
              <a href="https://onedrive.live.com/" rel="noopener" target="_blank">
               Microsoft OneDrive
              </a>
              and email you a link to its location.
             </p>
             <ol>
              <li>
               For "Delivery method," select
               <strong>
                Add to OneDrive
               </strong>
               .
              </li>
              <li>
               Select
               <strong>
                Link accounts and create export
               </strong>
               .
              </li>
              <li>
               You'll be directed to Microsoft. Sign in to your Microsoft account if prompted.
              </li>
              <li>
               In the Microsoft window that asks if Google Download Your Data can access your info, select
               <strong>
                Yes
               </strong>
               .
              </li>
              <li>
               To keep your data private, make sure you're not sharing this OneDrive folder with anyone else.
              </li>
              <li>
               In the email that arrives, select
               <strong>
                View in OneDrive
               </strong>
               . You'll be taken to the OneDrive folder with your archive.
              </li>
              <li>
               To download your data, follow OneDrive's process to download files.
              </li>
             </ol>
            </div>
            <div>
             <p>
              <strong>
               Notes
              </strong>
             </p>
             <ul>
              <li>
               After you follow these steps, Google Download Your Data will show up in your Microsoft OneDrive security and privacy settings as an app that can access some of your info. You can remove Google's access at any time. (If you export data to OneDrive in the future, you'll need to give Google access again.)
              </li>
              <li>
               When your archive reaches Microsoft OneDrive, Google is no longer responsible for it. Your archive will be covered by the
               <a href="https://www.microsoft.com/servicesagreement/" rel="noopener" target="_blank">
                Microsoft Services Agreement
               </a>
               .
              </li>
             </ul>
            </div>
           </div>
           <h4 class="zippy">
            Add to Box
           </h4>
           <div>
            <div>
             <p>
              We'll upload your archive to
              <a href="https://www.box.com" rel="noopener" target="_blank">
               Box
              </a>
              and email you a link to its location.
             </p>
             <ol>
              <li>
               For "Delivery method," select
               <strong>
                Add to Box
               </strong>
               .
              </li>
              <li>
               Select
               <strong>
                Link accounts and create export
               </strong>
               .
              </li>
              <li>
               You'll be directed to Box. Sign in to your Box account if prompted.
              </li>
              <li>
               In the Box window that asks if Google Download Your Data can access your info, select
               <strong>
                Grant access to Box
               </strong>
               .
              </li>
              <li>
               To keep your data private, make sure you're not sharing this Box folder with anyone else. If you are exporting to an enterprise account, the admin will be able to view your data even if no sharing link is created.
              </li>
              <li>
               In the email that arrives, select
               <strong>
                View in Box
               </strong>
               . You'll be taken to the Box folder with your archive.
              </li>
              <li>
               To download your data, follow Box’s process to download files.
              </li>
             </ol>
            </div>
            <div>
             <p>
              <strong>
               Notes
              </strong>
             </p>
             <ul>
              <li>
               After you follow these steps, Google Download Your Data will show up in your
               <a href="https://app.box.com/services/browse/my" rel="noopener" target="_blank">
                connected apps
               </a>
               as an app that can access some of your info. You can remove Google's access at any time. (If you export data to Box in the future, you'll need to give Google access again.)
              </li>
              <li>
               Your selected max archive size will decrease if your Box account's max file upload size is smaller. Files in your archives that are larger than your Box account's max file upload size will not be exported to Box.
              </li>
              <li>
               When your archive reaches Box, Google is no longer responsible for it. Your archive will be covered by the
               <a href="https://www.box.com/legal/privacypolicy" rel="noopener" target="_blank">
                Box Privacy Policy
               </a>
               .
              </li>
             </ul>
            </div>
           </div>
           <h3>
            Export type
           </h3>
           <h4 class="zippy">
            One-time archive
           </h4>
           <div>
            <p>
             Create a single archive of your selected data.
            </p>
            <p>
             <strong>
              Note
             </strong>
             : If you’re enrolled in the
             <a href="https://landing.google.com/advancedprotection/" rel="noopener">
              Advanced Protection Program
             </a>
             , your archive will be scheduled for two days in the future.
            </p>
           </div>
           <h4 class="zippy">
            <a id="scheduled-export" name="scheduled-export">
            </a>
            Scheduled exports
           </h4>
           <div>
            <p>
             Automatically create an archive of your selected data every 2 months for one year. The first archive will be created immediately.
            </p>
            <p>
             <strong>
              Note
             </strong>
             : If you’re enrolled in the
             <a href="https://landing.google.com/advancedprotection/" rel="noopener">
              Advanced Protection Program
             </a>
             , scheduled exports aren’t available.
            </p>
           </div>
           <h3>
            File type
           </h3>
           <h4 class="zippy">
            Zip files
           </h4>
           <div>
            <p>
             These files can be opened on almost any computer.
            </p>
           </div>
           <h4 class="zippy">
            Tgz files
           </h4>
           <div>
            <p>
             You may need additional software to open these files on Windows.
            </p>
           </div>
           <h3>
            Archive size
           </h3>
           <p>
            Choose the maximum size archive you want to create. If the data you’re downloading is larger than this size, multiple archives will be created.
           </p>
           <h2>
            Step 3: Get your Google data archive
           </h2>
           <p>
            When your archive is created by using one of these options, we'll email you a link to its location. Depending on the amount of information in your account, this process could take from a few minutes to a few days. Most people get the link to their archive the same day that they request it.
           </p>
           <p>
            <strong>
             Note:
            </strong>
            If you’re enrolled in the Advanced Protection Program, your archive will be scheduled for two days in the future.
           </p>
           <h2>
            Data you've deleted
           </h2>
           <div>
            <p>
             When you delete data, we follow a process described in the Google
             <a href="https://policies.google.com/technologies/retention" rel="noopener" target="_blank">
              Privacy Policy
             </a>
             to safely and completely remove it from your account. First, deleted activity is immediately removed from view and no longer used to personalize your Google experience. Then, we begin a process designed to safely and completely delete the data from our storage systems.
            </p>
            <p>
             Data such as
             <a href="http://myactivity.google.com" rel="noopener" target="_blank">
              items from My Activity
             </a>
             ,
             <a href="/photos/answer/6128858">
              photos
             </a>
             , or
             <a href="/docs/answer/6023494">
              documents
             </a>
             that are still in the process of being deleted are not included in your archive.
            </p>
           </div>
           <div>
            <p>
             <strong>
              Important
             </strong>
             : If the info that you look for isn’t available with these tools, you can
             <a href="/accounts/answer/3024190#data-access" rel="noopener">
              submit a data access request
             </a>
             . If the info has been deleted from our storage systems, it can no longer be recovered.
            </p>
           </div>
           <h2>
            Common questions
           </h2>
           <div>
            <div>
             <div>
              <p>
               If the info you're looking for is not available via these tools,
               <a href="/policies/contact/sar">
                submit a data access request
               </a>
               and specify:
              </p>
              <ul>
               <li>
                The categories of personal info you're seeking;
               </li>
               <li>
                The products or services to which the data relates;
               </li>
               <li>
                Any approximate dates when you think the data may have been collected by Google.
               </li>
              </ul>
              <p>
               You’ll need to
               <a href="http://accounts.google.com" rel="noopener" target="_blank">
                sign in to your Google Account
               </a>
               to complete the form.
              </p>
              <p>
               <strong>
                Important:
               </strong>
               You can also call our toll-free number, 855-548-2777. Our representatives can answer many of your questions and help you fill out the
               <a href="/policies/contact/sar">
                web-form
               </a>
               to ensure we are providing information to the account owner.
              </p>
             </div>
            </div>
           </div>
           <a class="zippy" name="format">
            Which format should I choose for my data?
           </a>
           <div>
            Deciding what format you should choose depends on the service, type of data, and your intended use of it. We have chosen types that we believe are the most useful and portable. For example, we export contacts as vCard, which is a very common format for email providers. We often will also provide additional options to fit your specific needs.
           </div>
           <a class="zippy" name="store_data">
            Where should I store my data?
           </a>
           <div>
            <div>
             <p>
              You can store your data anywhere that is safe and has enough room for it. In most cases, it is easiest to download it directly to your computer.
             </p>
             <p>
              If you use a public computer, store it in Google Drive or an alternate storage space where you are the only user.
             </p>
            </div>
            <p>
             <strong>
              Note:
             </strong>
             If you use Google Drive and plan to delete your Google Account, you'll have to move your archive to a different storage space before deleting your account.
            </p>
           </div>
           <a class="zippy" name="mult_files">
            Why was my archive broken into multiple files?
           </a>
           <div>
            <div>
             <p>
              Archives that are larger than the size limit you selected are split into multiple files.
             </p>
             <p>
              To decrease the possibility that your archive will be split, you can select the 50GB size limit.
             </p>
            </div>
            <p>
             <strong>
              Note:
             </strong>
             Special software may be required to unpack a tgz archive. Keep in mind that these types of files can't have unicode characters in the file names.
            </p>
           </div>
           <a class="zippy" name="expire">
            Why do my archives expire?
           </a>
           <div>
            <div>
             <p>
              Your archive expires in about 7 days. After that time, you'll want to create a new archive with your most up-to-date information.
             </p>
             <p>
              An expired archive doesn't mean your data has expired, and you won't experience any change in Google services as a result.
             </p>
            </div>
            <p>
             <strong>
              Note:
             </strong>
             We only allow each archive to be downloaded 5 times; after that, please request another archive.
            </p>
           </div>
           <a class="zippy" name="pw">
            Why do I have to enter my password again when I try to download my archive?
           </a>
           <div>
            <div>
             <p>
              The security of your data is very important, so when you create an archive, we want to make sure that you're the only person downloading your data.
             </p>
             <p>
              To do that, we ask you to re-enter your Google Account password if you haven't recently. We understand that this may be inconvenient, but it's important to take extra steps to keep your data safe.
             </p>
            </div>
            <p>
             <strong>
              Note
             </strong>
             : If your account has 2-Step Verification turned on, you may also be asked to complete an additional verification step.
            </p>
           </div>
           <a class="zippy" name="not_work">
            Why didn't my archive work?
           </a>
           <div>
            <p>
             If something goes wrong with your archive or you're not able to make one, try creating another one. This approach often fixes the problem.
            </p>
           </div>
           <a class="zippy" name="recent_changes">
            Why are some recent changes not included in my archive?
           </a>
           <div>
            <p>
             The file may not include changes made to your data between when you request a download and when the archive is created. Some examples include:
            </p>
            <ul>
             <li>
              Changes to sharing type or permissions for a Drive file
             </li>
             <li>
              Resolved comments on a Drive file
             </li>
             <li>
              Added or deleted photos or albums
             </li>
            </ul>
           </div>
           <a class="zippy" name="Gmail_labels">
            How do I preserve my Gmail labels if I am exporting my mail?
           </a>
           <div>
            <p>
             When you export your mail from Gmail, each message's labels are preserved in a special X-Gmail-Labels header in your download file. While no mail client recognizes this header now, most mail clients allow for extensions to be written that could make use of the labels.
            </p>
           </div>
           <a class="zippy" name="YouTube_videos1">
            Why can't I find some of my YouTube videos?
           </a>
           <div>
            <div>
             <div>
              <p>
               If you aren’t able to download some of your YouTube videos, check to find out if your YouTube channel is linked to a
               <a href="/youtube/answer/9367690" rel="noopener">
                Brand Account
               </a>
               . If it is, you’ll need to:
              </p>
              <ul>
               <li>
                Make sure you’re signed in to the Google Account associated with the Brand Account.
               </li>
               <li>
                <a href="/accounts/answer/7001996#switch-between-accounts" rel="noopener">
                 Switch to the Brand Account
                </a>
                you used to upload the videos to YouTube.
               </li>
              </ul>
             </div>
             <p>
              <strong>
               Tip:
              </strong>
              If you have more than one Brand Account, you can repeat these steps to download videos from your other Brand Accounts.
             </p>
            </div>
           </div>
           <h2>
            <strong>
             Common Google data download questions
            </strong>
           </h2>
           <a class="zippy" name="YouTube_videos">
            Which format is used when I download my YouTube videos?
           </a>
           <div>
            <p>
             Videos are downloaded in their original format, or as MP4 files with H264 video and AAC audio.
            </p>
           </div>
           <a class="zippy" name="Groups_askmod">
            I'm a member of a Google Group. How can I download messages and membership info from the group?
           </a>
           <div>
            <div>
             <p>
              Only owners can download a group's messages and membership.
             </p>
             <p>
              If you're a member or manager, ask the owner to download the info you want and share it with you. Or, if you get messages delivered to your email, you can download your history of messages from your email archive.
             </p>
            </div>
           </div>
           <a class="zippy" name="org_data">
            I'm a G Suite administrator. How do I export my organization's data?
           </a>
           <div>
            <p>
             You can download or migrate your organization’s data, including emails, calendars, documents, and sites. Learn how to
             <a href="/a/answer/100458">
              export your organization's G Suite data
             </a>
             .
            </p>
           </div>
           <h2>
            <a id="send-feedback" name="send-feedback">
            </a>
            Send us feedback
           </h2>
           <p>
            <a href="/accounts/contact/takeout_feedback">
             Let us know about your experience
            </a>
            downloading your Google data. By sharing your feedback, you help Google improve this product for you and other people.
           </p>
          </div>
         </div>
        </section>

              Get a summary of data in your Google Account
             </a>
            </li>
            <li>
